Welcome\n\nNOT\n\nUK,\n\nAugust\n\nCOMMrlq\'EE\n1, 1989\n\nRemarks\n\nChairman\nBowhill welcomed\neveryone\nand announced\nthat this was the final meeting of the\nMAP Steering\nCommittee.\nHe gave a brief history of MAP: the planning\nstarted in 1976, MAP\nitself was from 1981-85,\nMAC 1986-1988,\nMAS 1989-1990.\nTwenty-seven\nvolumes\nof the MAP\nHandbook\ndocumented\nMAP activities\nand scientific\nachievements\nreported\nat symposia\nand\nworkshops.\nThe participants\nintroduced\nthemselves.\nDr. Geller led the discussion\nfor transition\ninto\nSTEP.\n2. Approval\nof Agenda\nThe Agenda was\n\napproved.\n\n3. Minutes of 1988 Meeting\nThe Minutes\nof the 1988 Meeting in Espoo were approved\nreport which was given by M. D. Yamanaka\n(not M. Yamamoto).\n4. Committee\n\nwith the correction\n\nto the AMA\n\nReports\n\nData Management\n- Dr. Hirota reported\nlimited responses\nto requests\nfor inputs to a MAP\nCatalogue.\nOnly USSR,\nFinland,\nCzechoslovakia,\nFrance\nand Japan responded\nwith a total\nnumber\nof 60 subjects.\nDr. Bowhill\nasked if the Japanese\nData Book had been received\nby\neveryone.\nThe Secretariat\nwill send requests\nagain to every country\nfor data and letter of interest\nwith replies due by October 31.\nPublications\n- A list of the remaining\nMAP Handbooks\nto be published\nis given in\nAppendix\nI. It was decided that MAP Data Management\ninformation\nshould be given in the final\nplanned\nvolume\nNo. 32. Concerning\nMAP Handbook\nVolume\n32, the draft of the volume,\ncirculated\nearlier\nto the Steering\nCommittee,\nwas discussed.\nIt was noticed\nthat the format of\nRecommendations\nin Chapter\n6 was different\nfrom the other chapters.\nThis will be corrected.\nDr.\nBowhill will prepare Chapter\n1 and emphasize\nthe difference\nof the contents\nin the MAP Planning\nDocument\nand Volume 32.\n5. Project Reports\nATMAP\n- The report is given in Appendix\n2.\nNIEO - Dr. Kato gave the report and it is given in Appendix\n3.\nMAE - Dr. Goldberg\'s\nreport is contained\nin Appendix\n4.\nMASH - Dr. O\'Neill reported.\nGLOBMET\n- Dr. Roper gave the report.\nCLIMAT\n- Dr. Russell referred\nto MAP Handbook\nVol. 22 as the final report.\nGRATMAP\n- Dr. Fritts commented\nthat no formal activities\nhave been going on since the\nHelsinki meeting.\nThrane reported on the DYANA\nproject.\n6. Workshops/Symposia\nThe following\nworkshops/symposia\nhave been/will\nbe held since\nMST Radar Workshop,\nKyoto, November-December\n1988\nMASH Workshop,\nApril 1989 (Appendix\n5)\nMAC-Epsilon/MAC-SINE\nWorkshop,\nApril 1989\nSolar Activity Forcing of the Middle Atmosphere,\nCzechoslovakia,\n(Appendix\n6)\nIAMAP/IAGA\nMAP Symposium,\nJuly/August\n1989\n\nthe last MAPSC\n\nApril\n\n1989\n\nmeeting:\n\n90\n\nInternational\n\nSymposium\n\non Middle Atmosphere\n\nStudies, USSR, November\n\n1989\n\n7. Evolving into STEP\nDr. Geller reported on behalf of Working Group 4 of STEP. He said suggestions\nfor\nprojects should concentrate on coupling mechanisms and phenomena that can be accomplished in\nthe STEP period. Dr. Manson commented on the relation between STEP Working Groups 4 and\n3. MLT network will be active in both LTCS and the Dynamics area of WG 4.\nDr. Chanin reported on the IGBP meeting held on July 30. Two issues were discussed:\nthe ozone issue and solar UV flux have to be in IGBP. IGBP is slow in getting started; STEP is\nalready working, but it is limited in duration. The project The Middle Atmospehre Response to\nChanges (MARC) will be proposed to IGBP by March 31, 1990. Once it is adopted, IAGA and\nIAMAP Chairmen will ask SCOSTEP to handle MARC. Dr. Bowhill stated that Joe Allen\'s\nviewgraph on the March 13 flare should be included in the report to IGBP.\nDr. Bowhill asked if other MAP projects should be included in STEP and commented that\nthe transition would be successful.\n8. Reports of Representatives\nof Countries\nReports were given as follows: USSR (Kazimirovsky);\nDDR (Taubenheim);\nAustralia\n(Vincent); New Zealand (Keys)(Appendix\n7); Japan (Kato); France (Chanin); Norway (Thrane);\nCanada (Manson)(Appendix\n8); UK (Thomas); FRG (Labitzke); Italy (Fiocco); Sweden (Witt);\nUSA (Geller). The report for Hungary (Bencze) is given in Appendix 9 The Secretary will write\nto National Representatives\nto ask for final MAP reports.\n9. Other Business\nDr. Roederer,\nSCOSTEP President,\ncongratulated\nthe MAP Chairman and Steering\nCommittee on having done a super job conducting the Middle Atmosphere Program and remarked\nthat the results will be appreciated.\nCo-Chairman\nLabitzke also expressed thanks and appreciation\nto the Chairman for his\nwork with MAP.\nA resolution from WG 2D of IAGA to transmit to the STEP Steering Committee will be\nprovided by Dr. Simon.\nThe Agenda and list of Attendees is given in Appendix 10.\n\n91\n\nAPPENDIX\nMAP\nTentative\n\nschedule\n\nVol. 28: Fourth\n\nVol. 29:\n\nfor remaining\n\nMST\n\nRadar\n\n1\n\nPUBLICATIONS\n\nMAP Handbooks\n\nWorkshop,\n\nAbstracts,\nNovember/December\n(in press)\n\n1988,\n\nPart 1. ATMAP\nis ended.\nWe are now moving\non to LTCS, a project\nthat focuses\non the gg..0.p.lJ_\nand the thermosphere.\nLTCS is part of CEDAR\nand WITS.\n\nThere is no\nbetween\nthe\n\n92\n\nAPPENDIX\n\n3\n\nReport on NIEO\nSusumu Kato\nThere have been the following activities relative to NIEO since last year.\n1. Visit to Shigaraki MU Observatory by Minister of Research and Technology of the Republic of\nIndonesia, Prof. Dr. Habibie, November 1988.\nMr. Habibie visited Shigaraki and seemed much impressed by the MU radar, staying with\nus for three hours. On this occasion he mentioned his strong interests in the importance of the\nIndonesian Archipelago which influences global atmosphere environment through intense oceanatmosphere interactions in that region. We discussed NIEO to play a role in understanding of\ndetail atmospheric\nbehavior of the region thereby contributing\nto the elucidation\nof global\nenvironmental problems.\n2. Seminar in Jakarta, March 1989, on Indonesia and Global Weather\nThe seminar was organized by BPPT (Agency for the Assessment\nand Application\nof\nTechnology) co-sponsored by Japan-Indonesian\nScience and Technology Forum, and NOAA, and\nattended by 30 - 100 people. Profs. Kato, Fukao (Kyoto University) and Sumi (University of\nTokyo) and two government\nofficials\n(Agency of Science and Technology,\nAgency of\nEnvironment) from Japan and Prof. Webster (Pennsylvania University) Mr. Hall (NOAA) and two\nother scientists from the USA participated in the seminar. Besides scientific discussion relative to\nocean-atmosphere\ninteractions, E1 Nino, tele-connection etc., it was informed that the Indonesian\nGovernment is willing to cooperated in scientific observation of the region relative to the earth\'s\nenvironment\nas that by ships of other countries to work in Indonesian territorial water. Mr.\nHabibie agreed and promised to promote the NIEO project on his side. He suggested us extensive\nsurvey on possible sites of equatorial radar to obtain the most feasible one.\n3. Science grant of Ministry of Education, Science and Culture of Japan for feasibilty study of\nNIEO.\nWe have obtained a Science Grant of Ministry of Education, Science and Culture in the\n1989 FY for doing a feasibility study of NIEO. A group of scientists headed by Prof. Kato visited\nIndonesia, Sumatra, Kalimantan and Celebes for that purpose in June-July and September-October\n1989.\nAlthough the NIEO project has been formally submitted from Kyoto University to the\nMinistry of Education,\nScience and Culture of Japan for funding,\nthere are, besides the\nconstruction funding, various problems as to the organization responsible for operating NIEO, the\nway of international cooperation in the operation, etc.\n\n93\n\nAPPENDIX\nMAP\n\nProject\n\nReport:\n\nMiddle\n\nAtmospheric\n\n4\nElectrodynamics\n\n(MAE)\n\nR. A. Goldberg\nTo my knowledge,\nno new rocket experiments\nhave been conducted\nto continue\nresearch\nin\nthis field since my report submitted\nat the last MAPSC\nmeeting and which appears\nin Handbook\nfor MAP, Volume 27, although\nseveral projects\nare in the planning\nstage. MAC/REP\nis planned\nas\na rocket series at Poker Flat, Alaska,\nduring autumn\n1989, and will be used to study the impact of\nhighly relativistic\nelectron\nshowers\n(>1 MeV) on middle\natmospheric\nelectrodynamical\nbehavior\nand chemistry.\nDYANA\nis a European\nprogram\nplanned\nfor 1990 to study global dynamics\nand\nelectrodynamics\nin the middle atmosphere.\nDECIMALS\nis a Swedish/Swiss\njoint effort to study\nthe neutral\nand charged\nparticle environment\nin the vicinity of noctilucent\nclouds (NLCs)\nplanned\nfor the NLC\nviewing\nseason in the summer of 1991.\nSeveral groups\nhave now joined forces to\npropose\na NSAS\nrocket\nprogram\nfor study\nof the relationship\nbetween\nNLCs\nand polar\nmesospheric\nsummer\nechoes\n(MPSEs)\nseen near the mesopause\nby EISCAT\nand MST radars.\nShould NLC-91\nbe approved,\nit would combine\nin a joint program\nwith DECIMALS.\nThere is also\nrenewed\nactivity\nin this research\narea within the USSR where new rocket\nflights\nare studying\nmiddle atmospheric\nelectric fields using the field mill technique.\nMAC/Epsilon,\nconducted\nfrom Andoya,\nNorway,\nin October\nand November\n1987, is the\nmost extensive\nrecent rocket\nprogram\ndealing\nwith MAE.\nSeveral\npapers\nhave already\nbeen\npresented\nat meetings\nsuch as the ESA Symposium\non Rockets\nand Balloons,\nLahnsten,\nFRG,\nApril 1989; the American\nGeophysical\nUnion\n(AGU)\nMeeting\nin San Francisco,\nCA, USA in\nDecember\n1988, etc. In addition, a special\nissue of the Journal\nof Atmospheric\nand Terrestrial\nPhysics will be dedicated\nto results from the MAC/Epsilon\nand MAC/SINE\nprograms.\nThe Committee\nfor Atmospheric\nand Space Electricity\n(CASE)\nof AGU has also been\nsponsoring\nsessions\nrelating\nto MAE and have coordinated\nwith the atmospheric\nelectricity\ncommunity\nto locate subjects of common\ninterest to both groups.\nSuch attempts\nat uniting different\ndisciplines\nwith common\ninterests\nshould have a very positive\naffect on progress\nwithin the related\nfields.\nThe IAGA Working\nGroup IIA on middle atmospheric\nelectrodynamics\nhas been pursuing\nsimilar goals.\nIt is our hope that STEP will continue\nto find a home for this discipline,\nand such a\nprogram\nhas been proposed\nto Working\nGroup 4 of that organization.\nFinally, a MAP volume surveying\nthe first decade during MAP is expected\nto be released in\nthe very near future.\nOne chapter will deal with MAE, including\na listing of proposed\nactivities\nfor\nfuture emphasis.\n\n94\n\nAPPENDIX\nREPORT\n\n5\n\nON MASH WORKSHOP,\n\nAPRIL 1989\n\nA. O\'Neill\nThe third MASH Workshop was organized as a NATO Advanced Research on Dynamics,\nChemistry and Photochemistry\nin the Middle Atmosphere of the Southern Hemisphere.\nIt was\nheld in San Francisco, CA, 15-17 April 1989, and was cosponsored by the North Atlantic Treaty\nOrganization\n(NATO), the University of California at Los Angeles (UCLA), and the National\nAeronautics and Space Administration\n(NASA). The American Meteorological\nSociety was a\ncooperating organization.\nThe Workshop directors were Dr. A. O\'Neill (Meteorological\nOffice,\nUK) and Professor C. R. Mechoso (UCLA).\nThe Workshop was organized into five sessions with oral presentations, and one session\nwith a general discussion. About 50 scientists attended the sessions and actively participated in the\nexchange of ideas that followed each one of the 30 oral presentations,\nas well as in the general\ndiscussion.\nSession 1 began with a review paper (Dr. M. E. Mclntyre) on current challenges to our\nunderstanding of the middle atmosphere, and was followed by papers on the seasonal evolution of\nthe extra-tropical middle atmosphere (Dr. A. O\'Neill), photochemistry\nof the Antarctic stratosphere\n(Dr. S. Solomon), and observational aspects of gravity waves in the Southern Hemisphere (Dr. R.\nA. Vincent).\nIn session 2, theoretical aspects of gravity waves (Prof. D. C. Fritts) and observations and\ntheories of traveling waves in the middle atmosphere (Prof. I. Hirota) were considered.\nThe\nimportant topic of data sources and quality for the ta\'oposphere and stratosphere of the Southern\nHemisphere was discussed (Dr. D. Karoly), and a study of coherent wave-mean flow interactions\nin the troposphere of the Southern Hemisphere was presented (Dr. W. J. Randell).\nDynamics and transport were the main themes of session 3. An account of the evolution of\nfinal warmings in the middle atmosphere of the Southern Hemisphere (Prof. C. R. Mechoso) was\nfollowed by a paper on the climatology of the spring Austral stratosphere (P. Newman). The socalled dilution effect in connection with the break-up of the Antarctic ozone hole was considered\n(Prof. R. A. Plumb), and data collected during the Airborne Antarctic Ozone Experiment in 1987\nwere used to place constraints upon the effect of transport on ozone mixing ratios in the south polar\nvortex during spring 1987 (Prof. D. L. Hartmann).\nSession 4 dealt with the potential role of HO x and CIO x interactions\nin ozone-hole\nphotochemistry\n(Prof. P. J. Crutzen), and with the role of aerosols and clouds in stratospheric\nphotochemistry\n(Prof. R. P. Turco). These papers were followed by a study, based on a threedimensional model, of transport processes in t he middle atmosphere of the Southern Hemisphere\n(Dr. W. L. Grose).\nThe session closed with an overview of future observations\nof the middle\natmosphere (Dr. J. C. Gille).\nThe last formal session of the Workshop, session 5, began with a paper describing an\nexperiment\nin which a three-dimensional\nmodel was used to study the dynamical effects of the\nAntarctic ozone hole (Dr. J. D. Mahlman).\nThe modeling theme continued with a paper on\ncirculation and transport in polar regions in spring, as diagnosed in a two-dimensional\nmodel of\ncoupled dynamics, radiative transfer and chemistry (Prof. K. K. Tung). A paper on the use of\ndiagnostics in modeling and observational studies (Dr. D. G. Andrews) closed the session.\nDrs. W. L. Grose, J. D. Mahlman and Prof. R. P. Turco led a lively panel discussion on\noutstanding\nissues.\nAreas that were identified for further research included (1) the physical\nchemistry and microphysics of polar stratospheric clouds, (2) the possible implications for global\nozone of heterogeneous\nchemistry on sulphate aerosols, (3) the coupling of chemistry, radiation\nand dynamics\nin the middle atmosphere,\n(4) sources of traveling\nplanetary\nwaves in the\nstratosphere\nof the Southern Hemisphere\nduring spring, (5) sources of wave activity in the\ntroposphere\nof the Southern Hemisphere\nthat could influence the stratospheric\nflow, and (6)\n\n95\n\nreasons\nfortheamplification\nofzonal\nwavenumber the\n1in stratosphere thespringinal\nduring\nf\nwarming.\nProceedings\nof theWorkshop bepublished\nwill\n(probably\nearlyin 1990) yKluwer\nb\nAcademic\nPublishers\nas\navolume NATO\ninthe\nAdvanced\nResearch\nWorkshop The\nseries. volume\nwillbeeditedyDr.A.O\'Neill Prof. .R.Mechoso.\nb\nand C\n\nAPPENDIX\n6\nReport\nonIAGA\nSymposium Activity orcing Middle\nSolar\nF\nofthe\nAtmosphere\nJ.Lastovicka\nTheSymposium on3-8April1989\nheld\nintheCastlefLiblice, zechoslovakia,\no\nC\nwas\norganized\nbytheIAGAWorking\nGroup "External\nII.D\nForcing\noftheMiddle\nAtmosphere\n"\n(cochairmenLastovickandR. UNIVERSITY\nOFCANTERBURY,\nPHYSICS\nDEPARTMENT,\nCHRISTCHURCH\nA. The\n\nAntarctic Mesosphere:\nElectron density measurements (project scientist: Andre von Biel) are made at Scott Base\n(78\xc2\xb0S,167\xc2\xb0E) with the 2.4 MHz D-region polarimeter observations of the differential absorption\nbetween ordinary and extraordinary components of the partially reflected waves. There is evidence\nfrom the results obtained of the occasional existence of a thin layer of ionization which has a\nmaximum of electron density at about 50 kin. The probability of observing this phenomenon\nmaximizes at local magnetic midnight (approximately\n0730 UT), and during the Austral summer\nmonths.\nSpaced antenna mode wind measurements (project scientist: Grahame Fraser) are also made\nwith the Scott Base 2.4 MHz radar. The Polar Mesosphere Summer Echo has also been observed,\nin the form of decreased lifetime (after correction for advection by the wind) of electron density\nirregularities\nabove the summer mesopause.\nThere is a strong semidiurnal component\nin the\nvariation of lifetime which results in a minimum lifetime with a maximum westward phase of the\nsemidiurnal tide. The wind observations have also contributed to cooperative global observation\nprograms such as the Atmospheric\nTides in the Middle Atmosphere\nProgram, the Global\nThermospheric\nMapping Study, and the Lower Thermosphere\nCoupling Study.\nPreliminary\nmeasurements of scattering processes using frequency domain interferometry were carried out over\nthe 1988/9 season.\nB. The Midlatitude Mesosphere:\nSpaced antenna wind measurements (project scientist: Grahame Fraser) are also made at\nChristchurch (44\xc2\xb0S,173\xc2\xb0E).\nThese observations have also contributed to the cooperative global\nprograms.\nA study is currently in progress on the comparison of mesospheric\nplanetary waves\nwith stratospheric waves derived from satellite radiance measurements.\nC. Ozone and Aeorsol Measurements:\nPreliminary measurements have been made in NZ and Antarctica with a multiwavelength\ninterference\nfilter direct-sun\nphotometer\nto assess total column ozone and aerosol content.\nObservations\nincluded the recovery of ozone content at Scott Base (78\xc2\xb0S,167\xc2\xb0E)\nin November\n1986.\n\n98\n\nAPPENDIX\n8\nMAP\nACTIVITIES\n- CANADA\nA.H.Manson\nThere growing\nis\ninterest middle\nin\natmosphere\nresearchCanada. particular,\nin\nIn\ntwo\nOntario\nuniversities\n(Western\nOntario/York) additional\nhave\nresearch\nprofessors,optical\nand\n(lidar,\nMichelson) radarMF)systems planned. Bencze\n1. Changes of solar and meteorological origin in the mesosphere and lower thermosphere\nThe study of the effect of solar-terrestrial\nevents in the middle atmosphere\nhas been\ncontinued in the Geodetic and Geophysical\nResearch Institute, Sopron, Hungarian Academy of\nSciences. By investigating the distribution of electron density in the lower ionosphere, it has been\nfound that connected with Forbush decreases and subsequent particle precipitation a local minimum\noccurs in the electron density profile at about 70 - 72 kin. In consequence of this the geomagnetic\nstorm aftereffect in the ionospheric absorption of LF radio waves is modified appearing at the low\nfrequency end of the range, but decreasing with increasing frequency.\nA study of the effect of interplanetary phenomena on the ionospheric absorption of radio\nwaves indicates that shock related magnetic clouds are more efficient in producing\nstorm\naftereffect. In this respect the plasma parameters of magnetic clouds have also been studied.\n2. Turbulence\nThe method developed\nfor the determination\nof turbulent parameters\nin the lower\nthermosphere based on sporadic E parameters in the Geodetic and Geophysical Research Institute,\nSopron, Hungarian Academy of Sciences has been used for the determination of the vertical shear\nof the horizontal wind. Assuming saturation of the gravity waves producing the wind shear, the\nvertical wavelength of these waves can be determined.\nIn the lower thermosphere\nthe diurnal\nvariation of the vertical wavelength indicates a maximum in the midday hours, while the seasonal\nvariation shows a maximum in the winter months. The vertical wavelength seems to decrease with\nincreasing mean wind speed.\n\n99\n\nAPPENDIX\nMAP\n\nSTEERING\nAugust\n\nWhiteknights\n\n10\n\nCOMMITTEE\n1, 1989,\n\nHall Library,\nReading,\n\n6:00\n\nMEETING\nPM\n\nUniversity\nUK\n\nof Reading\n\nAGENDA\n\n1. Witt\n\n1989\n\nioo\n\nMAP\n\nACTIVITIES\n\nIN AUSTRALIA\n\nOrganization\nThe Australian Middle Atmosphere Program was coordinated by a subcommittee\nof the\nNational Committee for Solar-Terrestrial Physics. The chief tasks of the subcommittee were:\n1. Stimulating MAP interest amongst Australian scientists in the early 1980s,\n2. Reporting to the national STP Committee,\n3. Setting up MAP Workshops at regular national meetings of the Australian Institute of\nPhysics.\nAustralian\nInstitutions\nInvolved\nwith MAP\nMAP activities were undertaken by individuals\nUniversity of Adelaide\nUniversity of New South Wales\nUniversity of Queensland\nMonash University\nCSIRO, Division of Atmospheric Research.\nPersonnel\nDr. R. A. Vincent\nCommittee in 1984.\n\nand groups at the following institutions:\n\nMAP\n\nof the University\n\nof Adelaide\n\nwas appointed\n\nto the MAP\n\nSteering\n\nScientific\n\nActivities\n1. Dynamical Studies\nA major study of the dynamics of the atmosphere between 80 and 100 km was\nundertaken at the University of Adelaide Research Station at Buckland Park using ground-based\nradio methods. Regular observations extending over most of the MAP/MAC period have given\ndetailed information\non the mean winds, planetary\nwaves, tidal winds, gravity waves and\nturbulence.\nThe development of radar techniques for measuring momentum transport by gravity\nwaves, and the measurement of turbulence parameters in this region have been two highlights of\nthis work.\nStarting in July 1984, the dynamics of the 70 - 110 km region at Mawson in the Antarctic\nwere studied on a continuous basis as part of a program run jointly by the Upper Atmosphere\nGroup and the Mawson Institute for Antarctic Research at the University of Adelaide.\nDuring the latter part of MAPMAC a study of the dynamics and structure of the D region\nwas carried out by the Ionospheric Group of the University of Queensland.\nA determination of lunar tides in the 80 - 100 km region using wind data recorded during\nMAP, was carried out by R. J. Stening of the University of New South Wales.\nDuring most of the MAP/MAC\nperiod B. G. Hunt of the Division of Atmospheric\nResearch, CSIRO, continued the development of a general circulation model that extended from the\nsurface to 100 km. The model includes the effect of land-sea contrast, breaking gravity waves,\nand solar diurnal variability.\nTheoretical studies of the Southern Hemisphere stratospheric circulation were undertaken\nby D. J. Karoly of Monash University,\nand by R. A. Plumb of the Division of Atmospheric\nResearch, CSIRO.\n2. Temperature Measurements\nMeasurements\nof temperatures\nnear 90 km were carried out at Adelaide and\nMawson (Antarctica) using ground-based optical methods developed at the Mawson Insftute of\nAntarctic Research at the University of Adelaide.\nSolar\n\nTerrestrial\nEnergy\nProgram\nThe majority of the programs described\n\nabove are continuing\n\nas part of STEP.\n\ni01\n\nConferences\nand\nWorkshops\nThe ongoing\nMAP activities\nwere reported\nat Workshops\nheld in conjunction\nwith the\nnational meetings\nof the Australian\nInstitute of Physics.\nThe at Melbourne\nin February\n1984.\nThe two most significant\nmeetings\nwere the internationa|\nworkshops\non the Middle\nAtmosphere\nof the Southern\nHemisphere\n(MASH),\nand Gravity\nWaves\nand Bencze\n\nGeodetic and Geophysical\nResearch Institute Hungarian\nAcademy of Sciences, H-9401Sopron,\n8ox 5.\n\nHungary\ntook\npart\nin NAP\nactivities\nby\nmeasurements\nand by\nthe\ninvestigation\nof\nphenomena related to the middle atmosphere.\nSix topics have\nbeen\nselected\nfor\nstudies\nduring\nthe MAP\nperiod:\nstructure\nof\nthe\nstratosphere,\nozone\nclimatology,\nstratospheric\ndynamics, electrodynamics\nof\nthe\nmiddle\natmosphere,\nchanges\nof\nsolar\nand meteorological\norigin in the\nmesosphere\nand lower thermosphere\nand turbulence.\nIn\nthe study\nof the structure of the stratosphere\nballoon measurements\nwere\ncarried\nout\nregularly\nat\nthe\nstations\nof\nthe State Meteorological\nService.\nThe measurements\ninchded\nthe determination\nof temperature,\npressure\nand humidity, as well as the direction and velocity of the winds.\nThe total\nozone\ncontent\nwas\ndetermined\nin the Central Institute for\nAtmospheric\nPhysics\nby Dobson spectrophotometer.\nThe study of the ozone data\nis part\nof\na complex\ninvestigation\nof radiation conditions in the middle\natmosphere.\nData of satellite measurements\nwere also included.\nFor\nthe study\nef stratospheric\ndynamics\ndata of ground\nbased and balloon\nmeasurements\nwere\nused.\nThe\nperiods of stratospheric\nwarmings and seasonal\nchanges were investigated.\nConcerning\nthe electrodynamics\nof the middle atmosphere the atmospheric\nelectric\npotential\ngradient and the vertical air-earth current were recorded\nat\nthe\nGeophysical\nObservatory\nNagycenk\nof\nthe Geodetic and Geophysical\nResearch\nInstitute of the Hungarian Academy of Sciences, Sopron. The study of\nthe\npotential\ngradient\ndata\nindicates\na\nrelation\nto\nthe quasi-biennial\noscillation\nQ80, showing a positive and significant\ncorrelation\nbetween the\npotential\ngradient in the winter months and the solar activity (characterized\nby\nthe\ninversely\n1989).\n\nsolar\nradio\nrelated\nto\n\nflux\nthe\n\nFlo,7) in the west phase of the QBO, while it is\nsoIar\nactivity in the east phase (Fig.l) (M_rcz,\n\nChanges\nof\nsolar and meteorological\norigin in the mesosphere\nand lower\nthermosphere\nwere\nstudied\nby means\nof\nground-based\nmeasurements.\nThe\nionospheric\nabsorption\nof obliquely incident radio waves was measured in the\nGeophysical\nObservatory\nNagycenk\nof\nthe Geodetic and Geophysical\nResearch\nInstitute\nof\nthe Hungarian\nAcademy\nof Sciences, Sopron. Investigating\nthe\nphenomena\nin the lower ionosphere after solar flares in this institute,\nit has\nbeen\nfound\nthat\nsignificant\nreduction\nof the ionization in the mesosphere\noccurs\ndue\nto galactic\ncosmic ray (Forbosh) decreases,\nif the plasma cloud\ndoes\nnot hit the magnetosphere.\nIf the solar flare is followed by geomagnetic\ndisturbances,\nthe\neffect\ndecreases\nwith\nincreasing\ngeomagnetic\nactivity\nbecause\nof\nthe decrease of the cutoff rigidity. Brown\nAlan Burns\nGrahame Fraser (contact\nUsman Khan\nBryan Lawrence\nMurray Smith\nAndre von Bid\nStephen Wood\n\nA.\n\nScientists:\n\nAntarctic\n\nBag, Christchurch\n\n1, New Zealand.\n\nperson)\n\nmesosphere:\n\nDuring\nMAP this department\noperated\na medium\nfrequency\n(2.9 MHz) partial\nreflection\nradar on Ross Island.\nThe observations\nyield observations\nof the vertical\nprofiles of electron density and the horizontal\nwind at selected altitudes in the height\nrange of 40-120 km. The common transmitter\nand transmitting\narray are installed at\nScott Base (78\xc2\xb0S, 167\xc2\xb0E);\nthe two independent\nreceiving and recording\nsystems are\ninstalled at the electrically quiet site on Arrival Heights.\nBoth sites are close to the\nMcMurdo USARP base.\nRadar operation will continue beyond MAP.\n11\n\n2o\n\nThe electron\ndensity measurements\nbegan operation\nin November\n1981 and data has\nbeen obtained for most years since then.\nA self-calibrating\npolarimeter\nmeasures the\ndifferential\nabsorption\nbetween\nordinary\nand extra-ordinary\ncomponents\nof the\npartially\nreflected\nwaves.\nThe most surprising\nresult has been the occasional\nobservation\nof layers of ionisation with a maximum of electron density around 50 km.\nThe wind measurements\nbegan in November\n1982 using the spaced antenna mode.\nThe measurements\nof mean winds and atmospheric\ntides have contributed\nto various\nMAP,\nand other,\nprograms such as Andoya\nRocket\ncentre of operations\nfor all three campaigns.\n\nMAP/WINE\nThe results from the MAP/WINE\ncampaign\nwere published\nin a special issue of the Journal\nof Atmospheric\nand Terrestrial\nPhysics,\nJuly/August\n1987.\nThe campaign\nstudied\nthe middle\natmosphere\nin winter\nin high latitudes\nwith emphasis\non the following\ntopics:\nLarge\nscale\nstructures\nand circulation\nincluding\nseveral\nstratospheric\nwarmings,\nstructure\nand composition,\nwaves and turbulence\nand temperature\nstructure.\nNorway had instruments\non board 10 sounding\nrockets\nfor studies\nof turbulence\nand electric\nfields.\nThe 10 payloads\ncontained\na number\nof\nexperiments\nfrom institutes\nin Europe\nand the USA.\nAll 10 payloads\nwere built in Norway\nand\nNorway\nhad the overall\npayload\nresponsibility.\nNorway\nalso contributed\nto the campaign\nwith\ngrot, nd-based\nradar and optical measurements.\nMAC/SINE\n\nAND\n\nMAC/EPSILON\n\nNorway\nhad the overall\nscientific\nMAC/SINE\nand MAC/Epsilon\ncampaigns.\n\nand operational\nThese campaigns\n\nresponsibility\nfor the\nhad the following\naims:\n\ninternational\n\nMAC/SINE\n(Middle\nAtmosphere\nCooperation/Summer\nin Northern\nEurope)\nstudied the\ngeneral\ncirculation\nand temperature\nstructure\nas well as waves,\nturbulence\nand winds in high\nlatitudes\nduring\nsummer\nsolstice\nconditions.\nThe experiments\ncomprised\na series of regular\nmeteorological\nrocket firings and ground-based\nobservations\nas well as four launches\nof sounding\nrockets.\nThe campaign\nwas carried out in June-July\n1987.\nMAC/Epsilon\nwas a case study of middle atmosphere\nturbulence\nby means of instrumented\nsounding\nrockets,\nmeteorological\nrockets\nand ground-based\nobservations.\nThe campaign\ncomprised\nfour salvoes in which all rocket and ground-based\ntechniques\nwere concentrated\nin time\nand space to make detailed\nmeasurements\nduring\nevents\nwith strongly\ndeveloped\nturbulence.\nDuring\nthe campaign\nperiod the ground-based\ntechniques\nwere exploited\nto map the general\nbehaviour\nof the middle\natmosphere\nduring autumn/early\nwinter conditions.\nThe campaign\nwas\ncarried out in October-November\n1987.\nBoth campaigns\nwere very successful\nand the first scientific\nresults\nwill be published\nin\n1990 in a special issue of the Journal of Atmospheric\nand Terrestrial\nPhysics containing\n21 articles.\nMore than 30 groups from 12 countries\nin Europe and North America\ntook part in the projects.\nApart from the scientific\nand operational\nresponsibility\nfor planning\nand conducting\nthe\ncampaigns,\nNorway\nhad
